  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1812d6ea-babe-48f4-82da-1621cdd65b90'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText3756689316025934357" style="display:none"><i>Steffi doesn't talk, but she has so much to say.<br />Rhys can't hear, but he can listen.<br />Their love isn't a lightning strike, it's the rumbling roll of thunder.</i><br /><br />Steffi has been a selective mute for most of her life - she's been silent for so long that she feels completely invisible. But Rhys, the new boy at school, sees her. He's deaf, and her knowledge of basic sign language means that she's assigned to look after him. To Rhys, it doesn't matter that Steffi doesn't talk, and as they find ways to communicate, Steffi finds that she does have a voice, and that she's falling in love with the one person who makes her feel brave enough to use it. <br /><br />From the bestselling author of <i>Beautiful Broken Things</i> comes a love story about the times when a whisper is as good as a shout.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Some of it is cheesy, in the way that all contemporary is, to some extent, cheesy. It is not unbelievable, however. The two characters do grow their r<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Some of it is cheesy, in the way that all contemporary is, to some extent, cheesy. It is not unbelievable, however. The two characters do grow their relationship, it’s not instant, and yes there is more than just kissing. Foreplay and sex happens in the book between the two characters. Hope this helps!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1784826021?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1784826021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2082320181675877457"><b>This book is just SO FREAKING CUTE AND BEAUTIFUL that I just...I can't even begin to describe the dorky smile on my face right now.</b> No seriously, I spent <i>so much time</i> while reading this just smiling. SMILING. It's not a complex book, it doesn't have a lot of plot, and I did feel the ending was a <i>tiny</i> bit rushed but -- omg it was Too Pure, Too Precious™ and my heart feels very full right now.<br/><br/><b>+ I loved how it featured both social anxiety and deafness.</b><br/>Steffi has social anxiety and selective mutism,</span>
  <span id="freeText2082320181675877457" style="display:none"><b>This book is just SO FREAKING CUTE AND BEAUTIFUL that I just...I can't even begin to describe the dorky smile on my face right now.</b> No seriously, I spent <i>so much time</i> while reading this just smiling. SMILING. It's not a complex book, it doesn't have a lot of plot, and I did feel the ending was a <i>tiny</i> bit rushed but -- omg it was Too Pure, Too Precious™ and my heart feels very full right now.<br /><br /><b>+ I loved how it featured both social anxiety and deafness.</b><br />Steffi has social anxiety and selective mutism, and Rhys is deaf. And ok may I just say it was so so well done I can't even. I <i>can't</i>. I have so many feelings about the rep here!!! I can't say anything personal about the deafness rep except (a) the author clearly had done a ton of research, (b) it matches lots of ownvoices accouns I've read, and (c) it was well written and encompassed SO many details about the Deaf community!!! I loved it. <b>And Steffi's anxiety was just A+ and so well done omg.</b> As someone who as severe social anxiety too, it was like so nice to see Steffi (a) on a journey to help herself <i>because she wanted to not because she was being shamed into it</i>, and (b) to show how dark and lonely it is to be attacked with anxiety all the time, and (c) to show S.A.D disorders don't make you broken and you don't have to become neurotypical to be fixed.<br /><br />GOD. IT WAS JUST SO GOOD.<br /><br /><b>+ The romance was so freaking adorable.</b><br />Steffi sort of views herself and Rhys as: the mute girl + the deaf boy. And I <i>loved</i> how it fit together. They're sort of shoved together at school because Steffi knows some BSL and Rhys obviously does so...boom. The teachers smoosh them together. AKA the teachers are the best shippers in the universe. <b>THESE TWO. THESE ADORABLE TOO.</b> Their friendship is cute and dorky and sweet, so so so innocently sweet at first and just ahhhhhh. It's not rushed or instalove and it's FULL of anxiety and awkwardness still.<br /><br /><b>+ OOoh what is this I see? GOOD PARENTS?</b><br />Steffi's parents are separated but, mate, this equals her having FOUR excellent parents who love her (!!) like wow. (Although Steffi's mum was really horrible at first and completely ableist towards her daughter's condition. ruhughughauRGUHG.)<br /><br /><b>+ Actually lovely female friendship!</b><br />Steffi's BFF is Tem and they've been close for<i>ever</i> but like...after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25437747.Beautiful_Broken_Things" title="Beautiful Broken Things by Sara Barnard" rel="nofollow noopener">Beautiful Broken Things</a> I was worried Steffi/Tem would get poisonous...<i>it didn't</i>. This is a GLORIOUS example of really really good female friendship! It's not perfect. It has problems. But they love/support each other. BLESS 'EM.<br /><br /><b>+ Muchly diversity.</b><br />Obviously there's anxiety, mutism, and deafness....but also Rhys and Tem are both POC!<br /><br /><b>+ Honestly there is not much plot</b>.<br />Which usually bothers me in books but this was SO CUTE THO. I did feel it made the ending rush because obviously dire things have to happen in the climax...and like there was freaking 10 pages to go and I'm like "THIS ISN'T OKAYYYYYYYYY MAKE IT BETTTTTER" like the emotional wreck I apparently am. <b>Dude, don't you just sometimes read about good people and want PURELY good things to happen to them?!</b> Me @ this book. But I still loved it. Luuuurved it.<br /><br /><b>+ Okay but Rhys had some really frustrating ingrown sexism going on there.</b><br />Just with his whole: but Steffi I must take care of u my dove. And I'm just like NO. SHE IS A PERSON, NOT A LOST SOCK. But it was addressed and I liked that Rhys wasn't perfect. Steffi wasn't perfect. They both displayed some subconscious ableism to each other at times...but you know what? <i>It was addressed.</i> Niiice.<br /><br /><b> + OH MY GOD IT WAS JUST SO CUTE.</b><br />what is this fluff<br /><br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: This is an adorable story about first loves and being scared of the world but not letting it bite you.</b> There's not "romance cures all" in here. There's no "quick fixes"...actually there's no fixes. There's help and support and change and growth. <b>I fully admit it wasn't fast-paced or like complex.</b> But it was SWEET and I just loved it so much. I ship this mute girl and this deaf boy and their language with their hands and hearts so bad.<br /><br />I've been so sappy in this review I just need to go read about a dark murder or something omg who even am I.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2082320181675877457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2669821811" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2669821811" />
    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2669821811?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=contemporary-read">contemporary-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2669821811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14838962278141905685"><i>
  <b>‘With lightning, you’re never really sure if that’s what it was; it’s just a flash. Thunder, you know. You feel it.’</b>
</i><br/><br/>I fell in love with this book at record time. It’s not easy to completely fall in love with a book in <br/>right at the beginning because there are so many factors affecting the story and so many things that could go wrong, but books like these make me the happiest because the fear of not wanting to finish it vanishes when you’re through with your first few pages letting you enjoy t</span>
  <span id="freeText14838962278141905685" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>‘With lightning, you’re never really sure if that’s what it was; it’s just a flash. Thunder, you know. You feel it.’</b>
</i><br /><br />I fell in love with this book at record time. It’s not easy to completely fall in love with a book in <br />right at the beginning because there are so many factors affecting the story and so many things that could go wrong, but books like these make me the happiest because the fear of not wanting to finish it vanishes when you’re through with your first few pages letting you enjoy the rest of the book thoroughly. <br /><br />The characters really are everything. I have my first glance of my characters and instantly know that they are too good for this world but then I observe the writing and realise that it is situationally perfect and uplifts the characters. There is really nothing wrong with this book. <br /><br />Steffi suffers from selective mutism among many other things, but now there’s a new kid at school who is deaf and she has been assigned to him because of her basic knowledge of BSL. And as we all know they fall in love. Stephanie can talk to Rhys through sign language without ever having to speak but she finds that being with Rhys seems to open her up. Both of them are great for each other and watching these two fall in love, and then admit it, is one of the most adorable things ever. <br /><br />Steffi wants to go to university and study about animals, she currently works at a kennel. Her parents, who are divorced and have remarried, don’t want her to go because they don’t think she can handle it. Her mother has never been particularly tolerant about her disorders, she used to act like Steffi’s mutism was something she does on purpose. Rhys wants to become a video game developer and as joined this high school as a way to push himself to get used to life as it would be if he went to college, meaning an area where everyone is not really deaf aware.<br /><br />Yes, this book has an amazing love story, the cutest characters, and a world with extreme potential for character development but what I love most about books like this is that it spreads awareness and brings attention to concepts that would otherwise be left unheard. There are so many issues put in the world that have never really caught our attention because we’ve never had to cross paths with them but then you read a book like this and your eyes have been opened a fraction more than they were and the world is just a bit bigger. <br />Not being aware can’t exactly be compared to ignorance because you might not have had an opportunity in your life for you to see such issues ever come to light. Then, by chance, you open a book like this, you read a story set in this world we love in, and you realise that no matter how small these issues are they are not be taken lightly, because to so many people out in the world it might just be the life they’re living. Books like these bring people together and also makes people suffering from something similar feel a little less alone.<br /><br />This book deals with a lot of things, selective mutism, anxiety, shyness, and deafness. The big guns. And then it also deals with simpler things like friendship, first love, insecurity, best friends, pets, siblings, family, and independence. You read this book and you acknowledge that it’s a love story but it’s being driven by so much more. Sara Barnard pulled all the stops while writing this marvelous story. This is the sort of book that everyone should read, not just for the awareness, but also for the simple joy of reading a beautiful story built on nothing but love.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>But I love him, and he loves me.<br />And that, among other things, is enough.</b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14838962278141905685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Lala BooksandLala" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31027440-lala-booksandlala"><img alt="Lala BooksandLala" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597009469p2/31027440.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1771467152?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lala BooksandLala" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lala BooksandLala" href="/user/show/31027440-lala-booksandlala">Lala BooksandLala</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31027440-lala-booksandlala?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1771467152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13775009868957532113">It should go without saying that my opinion of this book should not be taken as valuable when compared to a reviewer who is deaf or has selective mutism. I genuinely hope (and as is reflected in my note to the publisher) that this ARC also got sent out to readers who can identify with these characters and give their comments on how respectful the representation feels, as my thoughts of this book are simply not as important.<br/><br/>I believe when it comes to writing any characters outside of your own exp</span>
  <span id="freeText13775009868957532113" style="display:none">It should go without saying that my opinion of this book should not be taken as valuable when compared to a reviewer who is deaf or has selective mutism. I genuinely hope (and as is reflected in my note to the publisher) that this ARC also got sent out to readers who can identify with these characters and give their comments on how respectful the representation feels, as my thoughts of this book are simply not as important.<br /><br />I believe when it comes to writing any characters outside of your own experience, it is important to be sensitive to the people reading who will identify with those characters and to write the book FOR those people. If you're not writing it for them, you are exploiting their experience.<br /><br />With that being said, in my opinion this book was as incredibly written as it was respectful. I think the author took much care to not fall into tropes and cliches that often exists in books that are harmful to the deaf community especially. I am looking forward to this book being read by more people, as I am very willing to pay mind to other, more credible readers' thoughts on this story, and adjust my review accordingly. I will be making a full video review of this in the coming month if you're interested in more of my thoughts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13775009868957532113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2514158761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2514158761" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2514158761?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2514158761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17030829729827492388">there are two very important things you will learn when you read this book:<br/><br/>1) you dont to be able to hear in order to listen, and<br/>2) just because you cant speak doesnt mean you dont have a voice.<br/><br/>there was just so much to love about this book, but i think those two points were the most special, the most meaningful. and i love how they were expressed in a YA novel. its so important for people of all ages to realise these types of lessons, but even more so for teenagers who are at the stage in life </span>
  <span id="freeText17030829729827492388" style="display:none">there are two very important things you will learn when you read this book:<br /><br />1) you dont to be able to hear in order to listen, and<br />2) just because you cant speak doesnt mean you dont have a voice.<br /><br />there was just so much to love about this book, but i think those two points were the most special, the most meaningful. and i love how they were expressed in a YA novel. its so important for people of all ages to realise these types of lessons, but even more so for teenagers who are at the stage in life where they are trying to figure out who they are and who they want to be.<br /><br />i also thought the representation in the story was phenomenal. it so important for mental health, especially anxiety, to be portrayed in such a mainstream way to show readers they are not alone. i thought stefanies struggles were so accurately real, so it was encouraging to see her grow and take control of her life.<br /><br />also, i will always have a soft spot in my heart for the deaf community. i could count on my hand the number of books i have read where the main character is deaf, so this was really a treat to read about rhys (hes also welsh so that just makes me love him even more). <br /><br />overall, this was a truly wonderful book. yes, there were times where i was annoyingly frustrated with the main characters, but im usually annoyed by most teenagers in real life so i cant fault the book for that. lol. the writing style also took me some time to get used to. but in the end, i felt a very deep sense of compassion for steffi and rhys, and for every quiet person who can relate to them. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17030829729827492388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ❀" href="/user/show/49148508-may">may ❀</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1805594173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer770674671702415965">Spontaneous <b> buddy read </b> with this fabulous girlie, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/36873117-maram' rel='nofollow noopener'>Maram</a> <br/><br/>So to start things off, I’d like to mention that you should take my rating like <b> a grain of salt </b> because honestly I don’t know how to rate this book.<br/><br/>It was GREAT, it was cute and fluffy and heartwarming and very very very informative, but at the same time, I felt that it lulled in certain moments. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420522480ra/13235772.gif' width='400' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And that was a big deal for me because I WANTED TO LOVE IT SO BADLY AND AWARD IT ALL 5 SUPER CUTE STARS but I found myself zoning out or makin</span>
  <span id="freeText770674671702415965" style="display:none">Spontaneous <b> buddy read </b> with this fabulous girlie, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/36873117-maram" rel="nofollow noopener">Maram</a> <br><br>So to start things off, I’d like to mention that you should take my rating like <b> a grain of salt </b> because honestly I don’t know how to rate this book.<br><br>It was GREAT, it was cute and fluffy and heartwarming and very very very informative, but at the same time, I felt that it lulled in certain moments. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420522480ra/13235772.gif" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And that was a big deal for me because I WANTED TO LOVE IT SO BADLY AND AWARD IT ALL 5 SUPER CUTE STARS but I found myself zoning out or making a tab to watch a video or catch up with the news while I SHOULD have been reading!! And that’s truly not acceptable. <br><br>So onto the plot reals quick. <br><br>This is a story of Steffi, a sixteen year-old girl who suffers from selective mutism and Rhys, a seventeen year-old boy who is deaf. Fortunately for both of them, they can communicate in sign language (though Steffi is not as fluent as Rhys but they make it work). <br><br>So we follow these two lovable characters (especially Rhys, this boy is a cupcake) as they build a friendship and fall in love but love doesn’t cure all problems. The two of them will have to figure <b> that </b> out on their own. <br><br>The thing with this book is that is SO ADORABLE but also so real! Like when the author was describing how cripplingly it feels when you’re an extremely shy person and you’re in a social setting. Or how panic attacks can form out of <i> literally nothing. </i><br><br><i> “Panic attacks are a lot like being drunk in some ways, you lose self-control. You cry for seemingly no reason. You deal with the hangover long into the next day.” </i><br><br>IT’S JUST SO RELATEABLE !!!<br><br>Now why my rating is lacking you may wonder, well that’s probably my fault and not the book or the author’s problem but I just found myself distracted so often!! And it was really annoying when I wanted to fall into this adorable world but IT JUST WOULDN’T HAPPEN!!! *screams*<br><br>Anyways, im gonna go check out what else this author got bc im intrigued. <br><br><i> ‘With lightning, you’re never really sure if that’s what it was; it’s just a flash. Thunder, you know. You feel it.’ </i><br><br>3.75 stars!!!<br></span>

<div id="review_1972885256" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1972885256" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1972885256?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781534402416" href="/book/show/35297353-a-quiet-kind-of-thunder">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to destiny ♡⚔♡ by: </span>
      Kathy - Books &amp; Munches
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=disability-and-mi">disability-and-mi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1972885256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2328660422181925334">Huge thank you to my sweet friend <a href='https://booksandmunches.com/2018/06/24/review-a-quiet-kind-of-thunder/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kathy</a> for sending me a surprise gift copy of this book! She read it and loved it so much that she wanted me to read it too, and I’m so glad that she did, because it was so beautifully diverse, and sweet, and funny, and altogether just a precious story of friendship, love, and adapting to a world that doesn’t always meet your needs. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“I want the world, I think. Even if it scares me.”</b>
</blockquote><br/>First of all, the representation in this book: fantastic. None of it feels for</span>
  <span id="freeText2328660422181925334" style="display:none">Huge thank you to my sweet friend <a href="https://booksandmunches.com/2018/06/24/review-a-quiet-kind-of-thunder/" rel="nofollow noopener">Kathy</a> for sending me a surprise gift copy of this book! She read it and loved it so much that she wanted me to read it too, and I’m so glad that she did, because it was so beautifully diverse, and sweet, and funny, and altogether just a precious story of friendship, love, and adapting to a world that doesn’t always meet your needs. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“I want the world, I think. Even if it scares me.”</b>
</blockquote><br />First of all, the representation in this book: fantastic. None of it feels forced or thrown in just to mark off a checkbox. Steffi has selective mutism and severe anxiety (and I can say from experience that her anxiety rep is <b>on point</b> and I saw myself so much therein), Rhys is d/Deaf, and both Rhys and Tem (Steffi’s best friend) are POC (though I don’t <i>think</i> it was ever stated precisely what race either character was, so unfortunately I cannot give specifics on that). While the d/Deaf rep is not own-voice, and I can’t speak for sure on this since I am not d/Deaf myself, it did feel very respectfully done to me and I <i>felt</i> like the author had done her research. <b>That said, my outsider’s perspective on this representation will never be half as important as own-voice reviews for this book, so if you have an own-voice review that you would like boosted, please message me so I can link to your review!</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“I decide this is just A Bad Day. We all get them, because grief doesn't care how many years it's been.”</b>
</blockquote><br />Ultimately, though there are some underlying themes—such as the grief of Steffi’s deceased older brother, her struggles with her mother’s ableist views of her, and the difficulties she faces regarding going off to college soon—this story is heavily character-driven, so don’t go into it expecting <i>too</i> much of a plot. In fact, the reason I gave it 4 stars instead of 5 was simply because the second half focused so heavily on the relationship between Steffi and Rhys that I found myself getting bored at certain scenes.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> “Extroverts can be shy, introverts can be bold, and a condition like anxiety can strike whatever kind of social animal you are.”</b>
</blockquote><br />That minor complaint aside, something I want to talk about for a second here is the <b>healthy sex representation</b> being portrayed. Unlike many YA novels that depict a picturesque view of a teen’s first time as being all silk and lace and swooning perfection, Sara’s writing is much more honest: the sex in this book is <b>awkward in the best possible way</b>, and feels so realistic. I literally laughed out loud at how relatable some of it was. Many of you already know that my chosen hill to die on lately is that <b>I believe YA novels need to depict authentic, honest sexual relationships to give teens healthy goals to strive towards,</b> and <i>A Quiet Kind of Thunder</i> does that perfectly, because even though it’s clumsy and awkward and imperfect, it also clearly expresses that they’re new to this, they’re learning together, and it’s okay if it doesn’t look like the movies.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“Little victories are everything in a world where worst-case scenarios are on an endless loop in your head.”</b>
</blockquote><br />The only other thing I want to touch on is how much I appreciated that, whenever something problematic occurs, it’s dissected and dealt with. Steffi and Rhys both occasionally have some ableist moments towards the other (more Steffi than Rhys, I think), and Rhys has some occasional issues with fragile masculinity and unintentional sexism, but it’s constantly addressed and challenged. The only thing I can recall wishing was challenged further was Tem’s obsession with virginity, but it isn’t presented in a slut-shaming manner so much as personal choice, so I don’t have any substantial complaint to file against that one.<br /><br />All in all, <i>A Quiet Kind of Thunder</i> is a very sweet, lovable story about characters who are relatable, funny, charming, awkward, and genuine. If you’re looking for a slightly fluffy but also important YA contemporary, I highly recommend picking this one up, and I’ll definitely be checking out more of Sara Barnard’s works!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2328660422181925334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1777244924" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer14189544523997857807">I don't know where to start. I'd give this book TEN stars if I could. I loved Beautiful Broken Things but I think I love this book even more. A brilliant depiction of social anxiety, a swoony subtle love story that creeps up on you, and meticulously researched, respectful and just beautifully written. <br/><br/>This book is not only for the quiet ones, but by JOVE how the quiet ones will adore this book. </span>

<div id="review_1917289558" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1917289558" />
    <a title="mxa ☂︎" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36873117-mxa"><img alt="mxa ☂︎" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595455725p2/36873117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1917289558?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mxa ☂︎" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mxa ☂︎" href="/user/show/36873117-mxa">mxa ☂︎</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=2017-releases">2017-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=short-story">short-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=babes-favs">babes-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873117-mxa?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1917289558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6110531795122823599"><i>Coincidental buddy read with the ever-so-lovely, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508' rel='nofollow noopener'>мαүғℓσωεя</a></i><br/>---------------------------------<br/><b>WOW.</b> This book is magnificent! Oh my gosh... The synopsis <b>DID NOT</b> display the care and attention that Sarah Barnard gave to her main + side characters. I'm surely convinced that this is some sort of a trick where the author just wants her readers to "pick it up" whenever we need a "cute fluff", so we always end up diving in with little to no expectation or at least be <i>okay</i> with it if it's not that good. Ri</span>
  <span id="freeText6110531795122823599" style="display:none"><i>Coincidental buddy read with the ever-so-lovely, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508" rel="nofollow noopener">мαүғℓσωεя</a></i><br>---------------------------------<br><b>WOW.</b> This book is magnificent! Oh my gosh... The synopsis <b>DID NOT</b> display the care and attention that Sarah Barnard gave to her main + side characters. I'm surely convinced that this is some sort of a trick where the author just wants her readers to "pick it up" whenever we need a "cute fluff", so we always end up diving in with little to no expectation or at least be <i>okay</i> with it if it's not that good. Right? Right? Well, I felt that and ended up being gutted yet somehow satisfied so that's why I'm easily giving this <b>5 STARS!!!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450115669ra/17379744.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b>The following points are what I jotted down before reading this heart-warming novel:</b><br>• I need me some cute, short contemporary to end the month of February with *duh*<br>• A male lead called Rhys? I'm sold.<br>• This looks so interesting! If it's done the right way, it would be such an honor to read as well as understand how a character that doesn't speak and a character that can't listen, bond and go through internal struggles together through their own means of communication. More so, what they learn out of it.<br>---------------------------------<br><b>
  <u>REVIEW:</u>
</b><br><br>'A Quiet Kind of Thunder' is an <b>adult contemporary</b>, broadly about two main characters learning to cope with their disabilities. Steffi Brons is a 16-17 y/o girl, who has been diagnosed with selective mutism since she was 4 years old along with anxiety, thus making it difficult for her to talk in crowds or any individual that's unfamiliar to her. For that, she is more comfortable in using BSL. Rhys Gold, on the other hand, is a 17-18 y/o boy who is deaf. We learn that he is seeking to challenge himself in a hearing world consequently moving in to the same school as Steffi and that's how, ladies and gentlemen, the cutest relationship begins. <br><br><b>'God, you guys are sickening,' Tem says, following. 'I'm getting diabetes just looking at you.'</b><br><br>I won't lie... there is an element of "insta-love" and I KNOW how annoying that can be, but the situation in which it happened didn't actually bother me (you'll understand why if you guys give this a chance, trust me! <i>
  <s>Oh and the pet names they give to each other are adorable!!</s>
</i>). What I can tell you is that Steffi and Rhys (just like all of us) are battling some major internal issues (be it something silly or not), and have found solace through each other. <br>With that said, this is <b>NOT</b> a novel equating happiness with being in a romantic relationship. It's more... the characters are learning how to <b>really communicate</b> not only with each other but their friends and family (I will further elaborate on this in the coming paragraphs).<br><br><b>
  <i>I love the entire Gold family, builds my confidence in everything from my abilities to my speech.</i>
</b><br><br>This story is also about family. I loved reading about both character's families and their massive support given to their children. Both families accepted them being together the first time around but also had minor issues here and there. Nevertheless, it's so beautiful to see them learn and grow from their mistakes. I especially enjoyed reading about Rhys family and how music is a <b>HUGE</b> part of their lives *Rhys can play the drums... <i>swoon</i>*. <br><br><b>
  <i>When we were kids, Tem and I went through a phase where we were both obsessed with pandas. Tem decided they were like us in animal form - black and white; cheeky and shy; lovers of food, sleep and play- and that was all it took.</i>
</b><br><br>That's not all though, this novel also showcased a strong friendship between Steffi and Tem. They've known each other since they were little and have always had each other's backs despite Tem moving out of Steffi's school. Tem may be Steffi's comfort zone/protector but I'm putting on a heavy dose of emphasis that their friendship is more than just that. <br><br><b>The writing style</b> is wonderful and easy to read. It also includes lists and text messages which made me fly through these pages wanting more. <br><br><b>
  <u> THE LESSON:</u>
</b><br><br><b>"Who <i>am</i> I if I can talk? Will that mean I say all the things I usually keep in my head? But so many of them are snide, or bitter, or just plain <i>dull</i>."</b><br><br><b>'But can <i>they</i> understand <i>you</i>?' Jane asks gently. 'Remember life is about dialogues, not monologues.' <br>I look up at her. 'Do you want to write that down so you can use it with your other clients?'</b><br><br>'A Quiet Kind of Thunder' teaches us not to assume things as well as to not bottle them up till they find their way to eventually burst. It's about giving permission to accepting who you are and what you're given. It's about communication being the key for any healthy relationship no matter what outlet you use. For that, letting out our innermost feelings are difficult but we won't be able to go anywhere if we don't find someone to share the burden with. That's not to say that we can't be independent but we're all meant to be living in this world. If people were more open in their minds and hearts, learn to trust each other then maybe this place wouldn't be so bad. Both of these characters are survivors and I commend Sara Barnard for delivering a book that's youthful, hilarious and in using catch-phrases to blend in with today's age and expectancies. <br><i>(It is oh-so unrealistic because things ended up working just fine despite the flaws but maybe, one day we can all be better too &lt;3)</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6110531795122823599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1977131016" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1977131016" />
    <a title="Sylvie {on semi-hiatus}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64899539-sylvie-on-semi-hiatus"><img alt="Sylvie {on semi-hiatus}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534779997p2/64899539.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1977131016?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sylvie {on semi-hiatus}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sylvie {on semi-hiatus}" href="/user/show/64899539-sylvie-on-semi-hiatus">Sylvie {on semi-hiatus}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64899539-sylvie-on-semi-hiatus?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64899539-sylvie-on-semi-hiatus?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1977131016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16045904476690140546">A Quiet Kind of Thunder<br/>by Sara Bernard<br/><br/>2.75/5 Stars<br/><br/>Br with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58818027-fares' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Pun Master</a><br/><br/><i>“Little victories are everything in a world where worst-case scenarios are on an endless loop in your head.”</i> <br/><br/>'A Quiet Kind of Thunder' didn't turn out to be the book I was hoping for. It was a nice book to read, quite enjoyable from time to time, but less spectacular than expected. <br/>At first it was still very interesting to me reading how Steffi and Rhys interacted independently with each other but also with their environment</span>
  <span id="freeText16045904476690140546" style="display:none">A Quiet Kind of Thunder<br />by Sara Bernard<br /><br />2.75/5 Stars<br /><br />Br with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58818027-fares" rel="nofollow noopener">The Pun Master</a><br /><br /><i>“Little victories are everything in a world where worst-case scenarios are on an endless loop in your head.”</i> <br /><br />'A Quiet Kind of Thunder' didn't turn out to be the book I was hoping for. It was a nice book to read, quite enjoyable from time to time, but less spectacular than expected. <br />At first it was still very interesting to me reading how Steffi and Rhys interacted independently with each other but also with their environment and made the most of their situation. What I also liked was how beautifully it was described the bond between Rhys and Steffi and how they fuse their worlds, deal with their "limitations", the aspect of communication between the two main characters was cute to be honest. What I most loved about this that it focused on mental issues without overdoing it, but it wasn't the most original story, I kept comparing this with other books, and tons of teen dramas happened most of them were unnecessary. <br />However, I appreciate the author for her effort, because she had a clue about what she was writing about (the mental issues and the disabilities that the characters were experiening or being diagnosed with it), and Sara Barnard has also tried to show that mental illnesses need more acceptance in our society today.<br /><br />A Quiet Kind of Thunder had a great start. In fact, I was so certain that I would love it, but I didn't. I liked the story and the meaning behind the metaphorical title, but the main reason why I gave this book a low rating was because of the characters, most of the times they were too problematic, but I won't give too much details due to spoilers.<br /><br /><u>So, about the characters:</u><br /><br /><b>Steffi:</b> She became a selective mute at a very young age, which lead to shyness and social anxiety (which isn't something uncommon). Something that very much bothered me: At chapter 20 or so, without seeing any progression our main character had already conqured and overcame her fears just like that, and because of that she became selfish and arrogant (two personality traits that do not suit her well).<br /><b>Rhys:</b> Rhys was adorable, kind and had a happy-go-lucky nature, despite he being deaf he could easily approch to people and interact with them, no matter how difficult it was for him. I can't dislike Rhys as much as the other characters, the boy did his best.<br /><b>Tem:</b> Tem seemed to be the best person in the whole wide world, the best friend everyone wants to have; cheerful, outspoken and energetic, but she never had a positive effect on her bestfriend Steffi. However, this circumstance has turned out to be rather counterproductive in terms of drama.<br /><b>Steffi's mother:</b> Steffi's mother confronted her whenever she got the chance, she kept putting pressure on her and making her feel insecure about her disabilities, which was not OK.<br /><br />The book could've been so much better if it didn't took opposite directions, and if the characters didn't make a major problem out of a tiny single issue. And if you don't like soap opera you'll certainly won't like this, because this was just like a soap opera but for teenagers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16045904476690140546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1805920850" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1805920850" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31923026-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533734143p2/31923026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1805920850?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/31923026-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1805920850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3213987242807185134"><blockquote>
  <i>Here are three separate but similar things: shyness, introversion and social anxiety. You can be one, two or all three of these things simultaneously. A lot of the time people think they’re all the same thing, but that’s just not true. Extroverts can be shy, introverts can be bold and a condition like anxiety can strike whatever kind of social animal you are.</i>
</blockquote><br/>Such a sweet story! It follows a girl who is selectively mute and her developing relationship with a boy who is deaf. The romance is ce</span>
  <span id="freeText3213987242807185134" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Here are three separate but similar things: shyness, introversion and social anxiety. You can be one, two or all three of these things simultaneously. A lot of the time people think they’re all the same thing, but that’s just not true. Extroverts can be shy, introverts can be bold and a condition like anxiety can strike whatever kind of social animal you are.</i>
</blockquote><br />Such a sweet story! It follows a girl who is selectively mute and her developing relationship with a boy who is deaf. The romance is certainly there with all the moments reminiscent of first love. But I found the book to be so much more than a story about the trappings of first love. It is an excellent exploration of both social anxiety and the hearing impaired, as well as the ways in which we communicate. The story does more than entertain readers, as it educates more than anything on topics like selective mutism, anxiety, BSL (British sign language), and more helping to enlighten readers on sensitive subjects. This is the most real depiction of social anxiety, let alone anxiety, that I have ever read.<br /><blockquote><i>Here’s the thing about anxiety: it’s not rational. It’s not </i>rational<i>, but it’s still </i>real<i>, and it’s still scary, and that’s OK.</i></blockquote><br />Steffi has selective mutism combined with severe social anxiety and has struggled with it most of her life. It has always been hard at school, but this year will be different starting sixth form without her lifelong best friend Tem beside her.<br /><br />Rhys is the new boy in school. He is deaf, so the school introduces him to Steffi because of her basic knowledge of BSL. We follow their relationship as it goes from strangers to friends to something even more. The two find ways to communicate through BSL, text messages, notes, and chat messages. Don’t worry though..this isn’t a story where they “fix” each other.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30197201.A_Quiet_Kind_of_Thunder" title="A Quiet Kind of Thunder by Sara Barnard" rel="nofollow noopener"> A Quiet Kind of Thunder</a> is about finding your voice and finding yourself. It is told in first-person from Steffi’s perspective. There are random lists throughout that cover things like 10 stupidest things people say to you when you don’t talk, how to look after your very drunk best friend, BSL signs handy to know, a snapshot of an anxious brain (things I worried about on the bus), etc. There is plenty of diversity. I loved Tem and Steffi’s amazing friendship. It may not have been the main focus of the story, but the strong female friendship was portrayed so realistically.<br /><br />I cannot stress enough how much I learned from this story. Not only is it very well-researched, but it is filled with important messages. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13857113.Sara_Barnard" title="Sara Barnard" rel="nofollow noopener"> Sarah Barnard</a> did a wonderful job at bringing this excellent concept to life in a truly relevant way. If you enjoy YA contemporary, this is a pleasant surprise. I highly recommend!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3213987242807185134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1779070847" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1779070847" />
    <a title="Maddie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18523225-maddie"><img alt="Maddie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531656548p2/18523225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1779070847?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddie" href="/user/show/18523225-maddie">Maddie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18523225-maddie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18523225-maddie?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1779070847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14049446282158280223">After reading and loving Beautiful Broken Things (so much it made my top fifteen books of 2015 before it was even published) I was so excited with Sara Barnard's next book. Now that I've finished it, the exact same thing has happened. This is pure gold (and bronze) and I don't think anything I write now will do justify to just how beautiful this book is. But, I'm still going to try, so here are some reasons to love A Quiet Kind of Thunder!<br/>Read more…<br/>Social Anxiety perfectly executed! <br/><br/>Steffi, our </span>
  <span id="freeText14049446282158280223" style="display:none">After reading and loving Beautiful Broken Things (so much it made my top fifteen books of 2015 before it was even published) I was so excited with Sara Barnard's next book. Now that I've finished it, the exact same thing has happened. This is pure gold (and bronze) and I don't think anything I write now will do justify to just how beautiful this book is. But, I'm still going to try, so here are some reasons to love A Quiet Kind of Thunder!<br />Read more…<br />Social Anxiety perfectly executed! <br /><br />Steffi, our protagonist, had selective mutism when she was a child, and now suffers from severe social anxiety and chronic shyness. This means that she struggles to speak in class and to other people she doesn't know intimately well. Her best friend moved to a different sixth form and all of a sudden she's left to fend for herself. There is this beautiful page that lets you into the spirally though process of Steffi and I related to her train of thought so much, I think I'm going to frame it to remind me that I'm not the only person that panics most of the time. <br /><br />If you liked Am I Normal Yet? by Holly Bourne, then you'll love this because it's almost like the inverse. Steffi has just gone on to anxiety medication (as opposed to Evie coming off it) and it really does wonders to her mental state. <br /><br />That's one of the things I was worried about when reading A Quiet Kind of Thunder. I thought it would take the same stance as Finding Audrey by Sophie Kinsella, and suggest that Steffi's recovery from her anxiety was solely based on the fact she had a boyfriend. It's not healthy to promote that you need someone else to love you in order to get better, and that's totally NOT what Sara Barnard suggested. Steffi is on the meds before she meets Rhys and is very aware that it's not just an influx of love that's helping her condition! Yay! <br /><br />Sidenote: Everything felt very sensitively written and well researched too! <br /><br />Romance so sweet you'll contract diabetes!<br /><br />I can't stress enough how absolutely amazing the relationship between Steffi and Rhys was. There was communication for one thing, even if it didn't involve actual words, and they really got to know each other before they dived into the lovey-dovey stuff. I really appreciate when love interests feel like friends, it makes the romance seem so much more genuine. <br /><br />As much as this is a story about finding your voice in unexpected ways, it's mostly about two people who are there for each other and complete one another. Not in a co-dependent way, but in a way I've never read before. For once, I felt that the characters were IN LOVE. I think that's down to the fact that the relationship is so well developed. They go from strangers to acquaintances to genuine friends to love interests and it's all a process. <br /><br />I loved when they met each other's families and friends and went on their romantic adventure to Scotland...it was beyond sweet, I had a sugar high for hours after I finished it. <br /><br />So, now you're thinking, is this just going to be 320 pages of pure joy, with no heartbreaking conflict whatsoever? Well, no... Steffi and Rhys do have some issues and its mostly to do with whether their love is real (I never questioned it) or just convenient because they're the only teens that know how to communicate with each other. It was a struggle reading about this complex between them that would drive them apart, but I'll tell you now that you can definitely expect a happy ending, especially when there are giant pink hearts on the cover.<br /><br />You need more reasons to love this book? <br /><br />I've never been one to mark favourite quotes in a book, but I put so many tabs in this one, it's insane. There were so many moments that had me laughing out loud, so many things I wanted to read out to Bee, and so many times I squealed and clutching the book to my chest, protecting my precious babies, Steffi and Rhys. <br /><br />This was an absolutely FANTABULOUS read and I can't wait to get my hands on a physical copy so I can hold on to it forever and never let go. It's a no brainer for me that this book deserved 5 stars, and definitely makes it to my favourites list of 2016!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14049446282158280223" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7231044600880120118">What a great book! Gosh, I loved these characters. Steffi and Reese just grow on you right away. I completely related to Steffi with her anxiety and her selective mutism, and the way it was portrayed. I loved the way the author contrasted how it was handled between her parents, and how this both supported and hindered her. Reese was absolutely a sweetheart. I liked the inclusion of little details like hearing speakers forgetting to turn towards the Deaf person so they could read lips, how frustr</span>
  <span id="freeText7231044600880120118" style="display:none">What a great book! Gosh, I loved these characters. Steffi and Reese just grow on you right away. I completely related to Steffi with her anxiety and her selective mutism, and the way it was portrayed. I loved the way the author contrasted how it was handled between her parents, and how this both supported and hindered her. Reese was absolutely a sweetheart. I liked the inclusion of little details like hearing speakers forgetting to turn towards the Deaf person so they could read lips, how frustrating it can be when medical personnel (and other people in public) address the caregiver or partner instead of the person with the disability. And overall, I just loved how he and Steffi had to work to find ways to communicate, not just literally, but in a couple-y sense. This was a great combination of a sweet romance and a book that was inclusive. <br /><br />Please excuse typos/name misspellings. Entered on screen reader.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1880123703" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1880123703" />
    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1880123703?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=underrated-gems">underrated-gems</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=great-reads-2017">great-reads-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=contemporary-na">contemporary-na</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1880123703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9013567443944999035"><b>*4,5/5 stars*</b><br/><br/>I think I died from the utter adorableness of this perfect book! Not only is it super cute and fun, but it's also intelligently written, quietly educational and very important and impactful book that everyone should read. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“They’re sprawled on the floor and chairs, talking loudly and easily, as naturally as breathing. Do they know how lucky they are? I catch myself wondering. Do they? Of course not. It’s probably the same thing someone with cystic fibrosis thinks about me. I guess</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText9013567443944999035" style="display:none"><b>*4,5/5 stars*</b><br /><br />I think I died from the utter adorableness of this perfect book! Not only is it super cute and fun, but it's also intelligently written, quietly educational and very important and impactful book that everyone should read. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“They’re sprawled on the floor and chairs, talking loudly and easily, as naturally as breathing. Do they know how lucky they are? I catch myself wondering. Do they? Of course not. It’s probably the same thing someone with cystic fibrosis thinks about me. I guess taking normal for granted is part of being human.”</i>
</b><br /><br />One of the reasons why this story ran so true to me was because I also had anxiety (I still do, but not as bad as it used to be in one period of my life) so I could see parts of myself in it, thought it was never as severe for me as it was for Steffi and I didn't have it since birth, for me, it started somewhere at elementary school and mostly centered around my class, or speaking in front of crowds and other places. So even though my anxiety wasn't severe, I could very well understand Steffi's problems and connect to her perfectly.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“And then it happens. The panic. It's slow at first, creeping through the cracks in my thoughts until everything starts to feel heavy. It builds; it becomes something physical that clutches at my insides and squeezes out the air and the blood.”</b>
</i><br /> <br />Other amazing character in this story is Rhys - who I completely and utterly loved, he was definitely my favourite! I also loved that this book educated us about BSL (British Sign Language) and even taught me some basic signs (yes, thank you, I'm sorry, I love you or family members).<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Sometimes, I just get tired of being me.”</b>
</i><br /><br />My recent encounters with more diverse side of YA Contemporaries - Made You Up, A Quiet Kind of Thunder, Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda - makes me absolutely excited to read more books from this genre featuring diversity, mental health, people of different colours and believes and other themes everyone should be more educated about. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“What are you thinking, Steffi? What are you thinking? Everything, all the time.<br /><br />You’re so quiet, Steffi. Why are you so quiet? But in my head it’s so loud.<br /><br />I’m sure everyone has an inner monologue, but I doubt many are as wordy as mine.”</b>
</i><br /><br />These books are not only far more important to read, but they are just all round more amazing than those boring and generic Contemporaries which in the end, educates me about absolutely nothing and gives me nothing new. So It's very satisfying to see authors writing more and more works featuring diversity these days.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“One of the things I both hate and love about BSL is how it forces you to be genuine. Half-hearted apologies just don’t work when you’re communicating with your eyes and your hands. You have to mean it, or it is meaningless.”</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>A Quiet Kind of Thunder</i> features greatly diverse set of characters - main heroines with severe case of social anxiety, deaf love interest Rhys (Absolutely loved him!), or best friend of colour - amazing girl friendship, interesting family dynamics, cute love story that feels real and <br /><i>*gasp*</i> love that does <i>not</i> miraculously cure the girl's mental health. This story was intelligent, heart warming, greatly researched and just overall real. Highly recommended.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“It’s not up to you to make my world smaller or bigger,” I say. “That’s up to me. But I want you to be in it. And I want to be in yours.” </b>
</i><br /><br /><br />--------------------------------<br /><br /><br /><br /><i>“The ten stupidest things people say to you when you don’t talk:<br /><br />10) What if you were, like, dying or something?<br /><br />9) What if I was dying?<br /><br />8) Can you talk if you close your eyes?<br /><br />7) OK, but what if I close my eyes?<br /><br />6) Cat got your tongue?<br /><br />5) Just say something. Really, just anything, I don’t care.<br /><br />4) Is your voice really weird or something?<br /><br /><b>3) You should just have a glass of wine.<br /><br />2) Just relax.<br /><br />1) You’re quiet!</b><br /><br /><br />“Here are three separate but similar things: shyness, introversion and social anxiety. You can have one, two or all three of these things simultaneously. A lot of the time people think they’re all the same thing, but that’s just not true. Extroverts can be shy, introverts can be bold, and a condition like anxiety can strike whatever kind of social animal you are.<br /><br />Lots of people are shy. Shy is normal. A bit of anxiety is normal. Throw the two together, add some kind of brain-signal error – a NO ENTRY sign on the neural highway from my brain to my mouth, perhaps, though no one really knows – and you have me. Silent Steffi.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9013567443944999035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1887195515" />
    <a title="Inge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6278820-inge"><img alt="Inge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556214992p2/6278820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1887195515?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inge" href="/user/show/6278820-inge">Inge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1887195515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2189497279549664768"><blockquote>
  <i>“My name is Steffi Brons and I don’t speak, let alone yell. I move slowly so people won’t notice I’m there, because running in public is as loud as a shout. I like to wear jumpers with long sleeves that go right down over my wrists and hands and fingers. <b>Meekness is my camouflage; silence is my force field</b>.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><i>A Quiet Kind of Thunder</i> started out really strong and kind of fizzled out near the ending, but I still really enjoyed reading it. The romance was stinkingly cute and I loved the addition </span>
  <span id="freeText2189497279549664768" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“My name is Steffi Brons and I don’t speak, let alone yell. I move slowly so people won’t notice I’m there, because running in public is as loud as a shout. I like to wear jumpers with long sleeves that go right down over my wrists and hands and fingers. <b>Meekness is my camouflage; silence is my force field</b>.”</i>
</blockquote><br><i>A Quiet Kind of Thunder</i> started out really strong and kind of fizzled out near the ending, but I still really enjoyed reading it. The romance was stinkingly cute and I loved the addition of sign language and the accurate portrayal of anxiety.<br><br>Let’s start with the <b>sign language</b>. I have zero knowledge of the language, so I don’t know if all of it is accurate. But there’s a heavy emphasis in this story. The conversations between Steffi and Rhys became mini lessons on how to say certain things, which I found really interesting. I also really liked the additions of the BSL alphabet at the beginning of the book and the signs for numbers above each chapter. It’s tiny things like this that really add to a book.<br><br>Then there’s the <b>anxiety</b> representation, which I have more experience with and was personally really happy with. Steffi has selective mutism along with a small list of mental health diagnoses, and there was one page in particular that really spoke to me, namely the one where she shows the inside of an anxious brain:<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487933471i/22065408._SY540_.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>I also really appreciated the fact that the book shows Steffi taking medication and going to therapy and actually benefitting from these things.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“Panic attacks are a lot like being drunk in some ways: you lose self-control. You cry for seemingly no reason. You deal with the hangover long into the next day.”</i>
</blockquote><br>The <b>relationships</b> were well done, too. Rhys can’t hear, Steffi doesn’t talk, and that forms a bond between the two that is hard to beat. I also really liked Tem, Steffi’s best friend, who was good fun and very supportive.<br><br>Also, THEY WENT TO EDINBURGH. It was a very short trip but really sweet, and it made me smile like a loon. I’ve never actually been to Scotland, but the country sings to my heart and calls to my soul.<br><br>To finish up, <i>A Quiet Kind of Thunder</i> has a few moments where it kind of drags, but is overall quite a strong book. Also, it has solidified the idea of me wanting to learn sign language, even if it’s just a basic understanding of things. I’ve always played with the notion, but never did anything with it. Let’s hope I don’t turn out like John Watson.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487933471ra/22065409.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2189497279549664768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
