<div id="review_2085081626" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2085081626" />
    <a title="Kate (GirlReading)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29599654-kate-girlreading"><img alt="Kate (GirlReading)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504444998p2/29599654.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2085081626?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate (GirlReading)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate (GirlReading)" href="/user/show/29599654-kate-girlreading">Kate (GirlReading)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=mental-illness-rep">mental-illness-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=2017-favourites">2017-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2085081626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13914451852041714471">4.75/5 *<br/>With it’s Disney, Les Miserables and Harry Potter references, diverse cast of characters, wonderful anxiety representation and yes, there was even a dog, A Quiet Kind of Thunder has everything I love and long for in a book. It had a perfect balance between the cute and fluffy, with it’s adorable, fun romance, whilst also discussing mental illness in a brilliantly real and honest way. Whether you’re living with anxiety yourself, know someone who is or simply want an insight into what it’s</span>
  <span id="freeText13914451852041714471" style="display:none">4.75/5 *<br />With it’s Disney, Les Miserables and Harry Potter references, diverse cast of characters, wonderful anxiety representation and yes, there was even a dog, A Quiet Kind of Thunder has everything I love and long for in a book. It had a perfect balance between the cute and fluffy, with it’s adorable, fun romance, whilst also discussing mental illness in a brilliantly real and honest way. Whether you’re living with anxiety yourself, know someone who is or simply want an insight into what it’s like, A Quiet Kind of Thunder is a book everyone can take something away from.<br /><br />*Read my full review here* <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://girlreading.co.uk/bookreviews/a-quiet-kind-of-thunder-by-sara-barnard-book-review/">http://girlreading.co.uk/bookreviews/...</a><br /><br />It pulled at everyone of my heartstrings and I think I’m somehow growing even fonder of this book whilst writing this. Looking back through the notes I took whilst reading, it’s even clearer to me how fantastic this book is in it’s discussion surrounding anxiety, mental health and everything that comes with it. It’s raw, honest, real and yet, it was uplifting. It had a brilliant sense of humour and a lovely romance to balance out the heaviness.<br /><br />I loved that, despite Steffi being able to relate to Rhys on many levels, there was always a reminder that Steffi isn’t deaf. It was made clear that she could and would get things wrong because, despite their similarities, their experiences differ in many ways and Steffi and Rhys would have to navigate that both together and individually, as neither could truly know what the other was dealing with.<br /><br />The diversity of A Quiet Kind of Thunder’s small cast of characters, adds one more reason to the list of reasons as to why this book is so great. In addition to Rhys being deaf and Steffi’s anxiety and selective mutism, Rhys is also biracial, with his father being from Guyana. And Tem, Steffi’s best friend, is Somalian.<br /><br />Sara Barnards writing style was incredibly comfortable to read, leading me to fly through it despite having been in a reading slump. I could have very easily devoured the entire book in one sitting had I not wanted to somewhat pace myself (an incredibly insistent episode of How To Get Away With Murder may or may not have been involved too…)<br /><br />It’s safe to say this book made my heart very happy and I would without a doubt recommend it to anyone and everyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13914451852041714471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I wouldn't let this put you off reading, though, just take breaks if it gets too real. x)</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1909919197" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1909919197" />
    <a title="bella farren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23223005-bella-farren"><img alt="bella farren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598064440p2/23223005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1909919197?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="bella farren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="bella farren" href="/user/show/23223005-bella-farren">bella farren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30981706-a-quiet-kind-of-thunder">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23223005-bella-farren?shelf=disabled-or-chronically-ill">disabled-or-chronically-ill</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23223005-bella-farren?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23223005-bella-farren?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1909919197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14151261339189240293"><b>3.5 / 5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>“Little victories are everything in a world where worst-case scenarios are on an endless loop in your head.”</blockquote><br/><br/>This was one of my most anticipated books, I had been desperate to read this after I saw that it had diverse disability rep, of which it had amazing reviews on. The deaf, selective mutism and anxiety representation throughout this book were so well done, there was no boy cures terrible and chronic anxiety here (and thank god for that).<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497449086ra/23024821.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Steffi and Rhys were both complex and love</span>
  <span id="freeText14151261339189240293" style="display:none"><b>3.5 / 5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>“Little victories are everything in a world where worst-case scenarios are on an endless loop in your head.”</blockquote><br><br>This was one of my most anticipated books, I had been desperate to read this after I saw that it had diverse disability rep, of which it had amazing reviews on. The deaf, selective mutism and anxiety representation throughout this book were so well done, there was no boy cures terrible and chronic anxiety here (and thank god for that).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497449086ra/23024821.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Steffi and Rhys were both complex and lovely characters, which is something very special when it comes to characters who have disabilities. I commonly come across (especially in YA) romanticised illnesses, and characters that cease to be anything but a walking, talking diagnosis. These two teens were not just there so an author could claim their book was ‘diverse’, Barnard clearly had done a lot of research and put so much effort into creating realistic teenagers and I loved it. <br><br><b>SO REAL QUICK,</b> this book focused on Steffi, a sixteen year old British teen who had been a selective mute for many years, stemming from her severe social anxiety. Steffi’s biggest ambition was to eventually go to university, much to her parent’s disapproval, and was determined to prove that she’s capable of handling herself despite her disabilities. <b>ENTER Rhys</b>, the new deaf student that gets paired with Steffi because she knows some rudimentary BSL. The two slowly get to know each other despite Steffi’s severe anxiety, and she slowly realises that communicating in BSL is actually something she enjoys and isn’t as anxiety provoking as speaking. <br><br>Steffi and Rhys were great, they each had their own struggles (although the book mainly focused on Steffi’s, with a brief few conversations about Rhys’ struggles) and the different way people can and can’t communicate. I thought it was such an amazing look into the struggles teens with learning/disabilities/chronic illnesses face in mainstream school.<br><br>This book was pretty wonderful, I enjoyed the characters and the every fluctuating relationships. But… there wasn’t much else going on. This was completely and utterly character-based, with even the character dramas ending without any climax (note: I didn’t want drama, but it just seemed to be lacking). High school was the original main setting of the story, with Steffi and Rhys meeting there, but that was kind of abandoned in the end as well. I just felt that the end was rather rushed, without everything having been addressed. <br><br>As much as it <i>was</i> cute and adorable, it also lacked emotion for me. I was going in expecting to be emotionally traumatised by this book, it had so much potential and I was ready for all the feels. But I got nothing. I truly, not even during the big ‘struggles’ got choked up, no tears were shed in the reading of this book. It all just began to feel a little superficial by the end. <br><br>There were a lot of cute little touches like the chapters headers including BSL (British Sign Language) signs and the little explanation of basic signs (I’m sorry, I love you, etc.). I just really loved that the author put in so much effort to immerse readers in the story and give us a little insight into SL.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449926042ra/17358929.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14151261339189240293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1856540018" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1856540018" />
    <a title="Puck" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18562856-puck"><img alt="Puck" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498403772p2/18562856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1856540018?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Puck" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Puck" href="/user/show/18562856-puck">Puck</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18562856-puck?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18562856-puck?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18562856-puck?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18562856-puck?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18562856-puck?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18562856-puck?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1856540018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2162073993519471583">An adorable contemporary romance, with sweet characters and great accurate representation of anxiety and being deaf.<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote> “Lots of people are shy. Shy is normal. A bit of anxiety is normal. Throw the two together, add some brain-signal error - a NO ENTRY sign on the neural highway from my brain to my mouth perhaps, though no one really knows - and you have me.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>This book is the story of Steffi and Rhys, two teenagers who both find it hard to live in the normal world. Steffi has selective mutism c</span>
  <span id="freeText2162073993519471583" style="display:none">An adorable contemporary romance, with sweet characters and great accurate representation of anxiety and being deaf.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “Lots of people are shy. Shy is normal. A bit of anxiety is normal. Throw the two together, add some brain-signal error - a NO ENTRY sign on the neural highway from my brain to my mouth perhaps, though no one really knows - and you have me.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />This book is the story of Steffi and Rhys, two teenagers who both find it hard to live in the normal world. Steffi has selective mutism combined with severe social anxiety, meaning that she finds it extremely difficult to talk to people and rather uses BSL (British Sign Language). Rhys is the new kid on Steffi’s high school and is deaf, and when the headmaster introduces him to her because she knows BLS, Steffi and Rhys slowly grow from strangers to friends to something more. <br /><br />So while the romance is a big part of the book, <b>A Quiet Kind of Thunder </b> is about much more than that. Apart from entertaining the reader, this story also educates us about sensitive topics like selective mutism, (social) anxiety, BLS, and the daily difficulties that the hearing impaired face. It is told from the first-person perspective of Steffi, which was lovely because Steffi’s struggle with her social anxiety was so realistically portrayed: as a person who also has undergone therapy to deal with severe stress, I completely understand what she was going through. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> I shake my head. “Panic attacks aren’t supposed to happen.” I say. “I’m on medication. I’m happy. They are meant to go away now.”<br />“Steffi,” Jane [the therapist] says, still gentle, still calm. “You know that’s not how it works.”<br />“Why <b>not?”</b><br />“Because anxiety doesn’t care if you’re happy or not. And if you tell yourself that you’re not allowed to have panic attacks because you’re ‘meant to be happy’, it will only make you feel worse.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />But it’s not all heaviness in this novel. Despite their disabilities, Steffi and Rhys still do normal teenage things together like go to parties, watch movies (with subtitles), and go on trips to Edinburgh. The story is also remarkably sexually positive and the author promotes safe sex in a very honest way that I haven’t read before. Steffi’s strong relationship with her best friend September (Steftember!) is amazing and very important to both of them, and there is plenty of cultural diversity in this novel as well: September is a black girl and Rhys is biracial (his father is from Guyana). <br /><br />As for criticism, I would have prefered a dual-perspective so I would understand Rhys and his problems better. Now the focus is mostly on Steffi’s troubles and Rhys falls a bit behind. The second half of the book was also a little more tropy that the first half – including a life-changing journey a la “TFIOS” – but Steffi and Rhys definitely are more than their disabilities and love certainly doesn’t 'fix' any of their problems. <br /><br />So not only has Sara Barnard written a wonderful love-story, it's also a very well-researched book about mental-health, BLS, being deaf, and the important support of friends and family while dealing with those issues. As an contemporary novel, “A Quiet Kind of Thunder” stands out in its diversity, dynamic characters, and well-build up romance, so it is a book that I would definitely recommend to others. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “Sometimes I don’t feel strong enough for this world.”<br />“Neither do I,” I say. “But we can be soft together.” </blockquote>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2162073993519471583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9782273278174990218"><b>5 heart-warming stars</b><br/><br/>Oh boy. This book. This book and its characters. This book and its contents.<br/>Diversity cast! Mature teenagers! No-romanticized anxiety disorders! Sexual positivity! Healthy relationships! Importance of friendship! No cheatings! No slut-shaming! Not <i>overly</i> fluffy and cheesy, just tender and important and heart-warming!<br/><i>
  <b>I loved this book to pieces.</b>
</i> And keep in mind that I do not tend to like, nor love, contemporaries. But this book truly warmed my heart.<br/><u>#BackstoryTime</u>: I suf</span>
  <span id="freeText9782273278174990218" style="display:none"><b>5 heart-warming stars</b><br /><br />Oh boy. This book. This book and its characters. This book and its contents.<br />Diversity cast! Mature teenagers! No-romanticized anxiety disorders! Sexual positivity! Healthy relationships! Importance of friendship! No cheatings! No slut-shaming! Not <i>overly</i> fluffy and cheesy, just tender and important and heart-warming!<br /><i>
  <b>I loved this book to pieces.</b>
</i> And keep in mind that I do not tend to like, nor love, contemporaries. But this book truly warmed my heart.<br /><u>#BackstoryTime</u>: I suffered, and still suffer sometimes, of anxiety disorders, and panic attacks, and let me tell you.. it's awful. And the way these problems are depicted in this book felt so real to me, I just.. ugh, I can't even explain how much I can relate to <b>Steffi.</b> The problem with anxiety disorders is that they do not just go away forever, and you can spend an entire beautiful day, and then, seemingly out of nowhere, panic starts and it's like you're awfully trapped in your own mind. This book do not make those problems go away the instant Steffi meet Rhys like <i>"Love conquers all"</i>, they do not magically evaporate, but the message is: you can best these problems with time, and you're not alone.<br />The romance made me sooo happy, <b>Rhys</b> (I'm fairly sure this name is given just to beautiful characters.) is just so cute and realistic, I loved him.<br />Maybe the ending was a bit rushed, but oh boy the whole book <b>was.so.good.</b><br /><br />Highly recommended!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2385765673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12078704534461222254">4.5 stars rounding all the way up.<br/><br/><i>He can’t hear, she doesn’t speak but they understand one another perfectly.</i><br/><br/>That’s the strapline on this book and it blew me away like I find the best YA can. This was one of the most relatable YAs I’ve read in a long time. I think some of this was down to the fact it was quintessentially British and not American and I loved the sense of home in this book.<br/><br/>Steffi was a carefully crafted complex and refreshing character. I ‘got’ her, I admired her and wanted her to</span>
  <span id="freeText12078704534461222254" style="display:none">4.5 stars rounding all the way up.<br /><br /><i>He can’t hear, she doesn’t speak but they understand one another perfectly.</i><br /><br />That’s the strapline on this book and it blew me away like I find the best YA can. This was one of the most relatable YAs I’ve read in a long time. I think some of this was down to the fact it was quintessentially British and not American and I loved the sense of home in this book.<br /><br />Steffi was a carefully crafted complex and refreshing character. I ‘got’ her, I admired her and wanted her to thrive in whatever way was right for her. Rhys was bloody adorable and flawed and adorable. Did I say adorable? *shrugs* The story of these two was an absorbing delight to read but it was real, it had grit.<br /><br />I devoured this book quickly. I slipped into this seamless writing with ease and I’m genuinely sorry it’s over. I will be reading more from Sara Barnard, she rocked this age range so good.</span>

<div id="review_2794644092" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2794644092" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2794644092?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781534402416" href="/book/show/35297353-a-quiet-kind-of-thunder">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=easy-read">easy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2794644092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer944626812552260178"><br/>It’s a very bold YA story in its overall sense. It’s very mature for a YA and the characters are very unusual, a deaf boy and a selectively mute girl. What I liked about the story is how it liberally addresses anxiety which anyone, differently abled or not can definitely experience. It also educates the readers on how the deaf communicates as well as how a girl with multiple anxiety disorder manages to cope. It is still a love story and sometimes it could get very cheesy and a bit unrealistic bu</span>
  <span id="freeText944626812552260178" style="display:none"><br />It’s a very bold YA story in its overall sense. It’s very mature for a YA and the characters are very unusual, a deaf boy and a selectively mute girl. What I liked about the story is how it liberally addresses anxiety which anyone, differently abled or not can definitely experience. It also educates the readers on how the deaf communicates as well as how a girl with multiple anxiety disorder manages to cope. It is still a love story and sometimes it could get very cheesy and a bit unrealistic but I think the author is just trying to take these issues in the most positive perspectives possible. </span>
  <a data-text-id="944626812552260178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2184857062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2184857062" />
    <a title="Julie Zantopoulos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51094260-julie-zantopoulos"><img alt="Julie Zantopoulos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503178209p2/51094260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2184857062?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Zantopoulos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Zantopoulos" href="/user/show/51094260-julie-zantopoulos">Julie Zantopoulos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51094260-julie-zantopoulos?shelf=diverse-read">diverse-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51094260-julie-zantopoulos?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51094260-julie-zantopoulos?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51094260-julie-zantopoulos?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2184857062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12457766113307070962">I'd like to preface this review by stating that I am not a part of the deaf community or living with the same mental health issues that the characters in this book do. As such, I cannot speak to the representation in the book, but it is my belief that it was handled fantastically. Again, that's from my scope and should never outweigh those in the communities represented. <br/><br/>That said, this book was beautiful, truly and wonderfully written. This book follows Steffi who is a selective mute with sever</span>
  <span id="freeText12457766113307070962" style="display:none">I'd like to preface this review by stating that I am not a part of the deaf community or living with the same mental health issues that the characters in this book do. As such, I cannot speak to the representation in the book, but it is my belief that it was handled fantastically. Again, that's from my scope and should never outweigh those in the communities represented. <br /><br />That said, this book was beautiful, truly and wonderfully written. This book follows Steffi who is a selective mute with severe anxiety that makes it difficult for her to speak about her peers, strangers, or in large social situations. She mainly speaks only to her best friend Tem and her family but she's working to overcome her anxiety and start speaking more. It also follows Rhys who is deaf and new to Steffi's school. The two are paired up because Steffi knows BLS (British Sign Language -as the book is set in the UK).<br /><br />The two form a friendship that leads to first love and discovering how they fit into the world around them and one another's lives. This book is raw and real and discusses a ton of important topics for teens and young adults. The displacement you feel going to University, the ups and downs of friendships, navigating your first relationship, sex, dating, love, and so much more. The family dynamics are messy and loving and Steffi herself-man is she a force. She's in therapy, she's trying medicines for the first time, she's strong and fierce, and the love interest doesn't "fix" her. <br /><br />I thought every aspect of this book was handled BEAUTIFULLY. Have I mentioned I think this book is beautiful? It's a recommended read for everyone I know. Honestly, pick it up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12457766113307070962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2193311593" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2193311593" />
    <a title="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer"><img alt="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553042105p2/7476091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2193311593?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" href="/user/show/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer">Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36130435-a-quiet-kind-of-thunder">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=g-c-british">g-c-british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=g-t-contemporary">g-t-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=genre-friendship">genre-friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=rp-netgalley">rp-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=genre-coming-of-age">genre-coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=genre-diverse">genre-diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=stars-5">stars-5</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=imo-worthy-love-interest">imo-worthy-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=fiction-young-adult">fiction-young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2193311593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer31475800735130638"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513291717i/24679810._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='279' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><i>Check out more reviews @ <a href='https://perspectiveofawriter.wordpress.com/book-reviews/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Perspective of a Writer</a>...</i><br/><br/>Steffi is selective mute and has been since a child... but that is about to change... she hopes!! This is the year where she's trying to break out of the hold her anxiety has on her actions. If she doesn't then her parents may just decide no university for her! Amidst this she meets Rhys. Deaf, they communicate through her rusty sign language. With her silent voice and his expert listening skills they become friends in their own little world, a</span>
  <span id="freeText31475800735130638" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513291717i/24679810._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="279" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><i>Check out more reviews @ <a href="https://perspectiveofawriter.wordpress.com/book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Perspective of a Writer</a>...</i><br><br>Steffi is selective mute and has been since a child... but that is about to change... she hopes!! This is the year where she's trying to break out of the hold her anxiety has on her actions. If she doesn't then her parents may just decide no university for her! Amidst this she meets Rhys. Deaf, they communicate through her rusty sign language. With her silent voice and his expert listening skills they become friends in their own little world, as they reconcile the real world around them there are unexpected twists to the world as she knows it!<br><br><br><b>The short review...</b><br><br>I LOVED it... ... ...What?! That wasn't enough for you?! Well I DO have a few more specifics about WHAT I loved... This has some masterful examples of family, a traditional one and a divorced parents one, both of which I LOVED and thought were spot on. The FRIENDSHIP with Tem! I NEED me my own Tem! And how cute is ASL?! (Or rather BSL since this is set in Britain!! Another bonus as I love the tiny differences in British culture as compared to American.) <br><br>I DID totally love Rhys! I love that his father came from South America and that he had a totally well adjusted life even as he dealt with his deafness and the emotions that arose due to how people treated him because of it. I related to Rhys but I HARDCORE related to Steffi's social anxiety. I really enjoyed how her counseling played a HUGE role in her getting a handle on her mutism while Rhys simply provided her motivation!<br><br><br><b>Cover &amp; Title grade -&gt; B+</b><br><br>There are two covers! I suspect one is the American version and the other is the British one. I really LOVE the pink and foil one with the type title. I was drawn to that one. The cover of my ARC is dark blue with hands in the shape of a heart. I'm less drawn to that one but I recognized the title right off! (Hence my grade!) The title is one of those old fashioned ones that are now classics. It's perfect as far as titles go for me... everything now is so literal and this one is simply beautiful poetry from the story itself! <br><br><br><b>Why should you read this YA contemporary?</b><br><br>The mental health, the mental health, the mental health!!<br><br>-The explanation of a selective mute was quite good. I felt like I came to understand this was truly an illness and that it was okay that it happened. We do feel like we need to understand WHY illnesses like this happen as if we want to judge whether it was something they did (like being fat) or if it is something that is "out of their control" (like our race). The message is that WHY just isn't the issue. It was beautiful and it was raw and the steps to getting healthier were laid out.<br><br>-Social anxiety which made Steffi's symptoms worse was also explored and was so RELATABLE!! Like really, really relatable! This is where Tem came in. She was the "normal," social one and provided a contrast to Steffi while also being integral to WHO Steffi was and how she had coped up to this point. There is this beautifully laid comparison between the two girls that goes a long way in showing readers who haven't experienced anxiety what it means to have it and how you can still relate.<br><br>-Then there is Rhys physical disability in his deafness. There is a helplessness to being deaf (or other physical disabilities) because this is something that is a literal part of you. As a reader you may struggle with that idea with a mental illness but we TOTALLY understand with the physical. So when Rhys struggles mentally due to being deaf we understand and we want to do something. Sometimes that is the wrong thing to do!! Getting into that mindset so realistically was a treat!!<br><br>-Finally there was HOW Steffi and Rhys coped... sign language! She couldn't handle the pressure of talking and he can't hear. They used BSL to bridge what they perceived was holding them back and to create a "safe" world to grow stronger together. That allowed them to finally step out from behind their individual fears. GAH!! It was so, so good... <br><br><br><b>As a Writer...</b><br><br>I have no idea whether Barnard has personally experienced any of these conditions or simply did an INCREDIBLE job researching! To me it doesn't matter. She tapped into the heart and supported each and every emotion and motivation the characters had... Steffi, Rhys, Tem and even her and his families! When you write the research is great but it must be woven into the plot (done, done, done!) AND it must ring true. NOT because the facts are all text book perfect but because we can relate and more, we understand!<br><br>I LOVE awkward people and I really enjoy that sweet moment when they realize here is a person that will stick by them... whether in friendship or love, it doesn't matter!<br><br><br>⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ Authenticity<br>⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ Writing Style<br>⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ Plot &amp; Pacing<br>⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ World Building<br><br>BOTTOM LINE: Diverse, British, mental health, friendship and romance!<br><br><i>Thanks to NetGalley and the publisher for providing me with an ARC in exchange for an honest review. It has not influenced my opinions.</i><br><br>______________________<br>You can find this review and many others on my book blog @ <a href="https://perspectiveofawriter.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Perspective of a Writer</a>. See my special perspective at the bottom of my reviews under the typewriter...</span>
  <a data-text-id="31475800735130638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=4stars">4stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=challenge-christmas2017">challenge-christmas2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=light-fiction">light-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=challenge-atoz2018">challenge-atoz2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2017">read2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2218506287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7173235137450418260">This is the cutest book that I've read since my beloved Lara Jean <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15749186.To_All_the_Boys_I_ve_Loved_Before__To_All_the_Boys_I_ve_Loved_Before___1_' title='To All the Boys I've Loved Before (To All the Boys I've Loved Before, #1) by Jenny Han' rel='nofollow noopener'>To All the Boys I've Loved Before</a> series by Jenny Han! I legit squealed a bunch of times while reading this as it was SO FREAKING CUTE!!!!! It was exactly the kind of cutesy, awkward teen romance that I'm a sucker for. Like okay... I know I was letting myself in for a hella amount of emotional manipulation from the get go because this is about a selective mute girl with anxiety who falls in love with a deaf boy..... Like it's got </span>
  <span id="freeText7173235137450418260" style="display:none">This is the cutest book that I've read since my beloved Lara Jean <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15749186.To_All_the_Boys_I_ve_Loved_Before__To_All_the_Boys_I_ve_Loved_Before___1_" title="To All the Boys I've Loved Before (To All the Boys I've Loved Before, #1) by Jenny Han" rel="nofollow noopener">To All the Boys I've Loved Before</a> series by Jenny Han! I legit squealed a bunch of times while reading this as it was SO FREAKING CUTE!!!!! It was exactly the kind of cutesy, awkward teen romance that I'm a sucker for. Like okay... I know I was letting myself in for a hella amount of emotional manipulation from the get go because this is about a selective mute girl with anxiety who falls in love with a deaf boy..... Like it's got the strings of the heart tugging immediately if you're in the mood for bubblegum light fiction. <br /><br />BUT!!! <br /><br />This is where I've got to give it major props because the issues surrounding Steffi's anxiety and mutism didn't just magically disappear because of love. Okay she went on this *journey* of healing with her relationship with Rhys helping her to blossom but lots of time in the book was given to her medical treatments (SSRIs and therapy) and the ending wasn't a love cures all ending. It was happily realistic. <br /><i>
  <blockquote>"I had a massive panic attack… It wasn't even triggered by anything I was happy... It's not fair..."<br />"You know that your anxiety isn't about happiness and sadness. It isn't a cause and effect. Sometimes, often even ,there will be very clear triggers, but not always. Chronic anxiety is a form of illness. It's not something you bring on yourself by how you feel on any given day."</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Time was also given to the struggles Rhys had with being deaf and what it was like for him to want to make his own way in a hearing world without being dependent on anyone for basic things in life that the rest of us with hearing take for granted. <br /><br />Also I liked how the families of both teens were present in this book. Okay they were rather perfect at times in their behaviour but Steffi's family dynamic in particular felt rather believable rather than the usual convenient parental absenteeism of so many YA novels. Her relationship with her mother was nice to read about in that it wasn't perfect and was a little strained but it didn't descend into overwrought dramatics.<br /><br />Steffi's BFF was an interesting character named Tem. Okay she did suffer a little from that best friend syndrome we usually get in rom coms as her storyline was really only there to further Steffi's. But she was likeable and fun to read about despite her clichéd personality. HOWEVER.... Oh however.... There was one line that she uttered in the book that I need to take issue with. It was rather a flippant comment but I think it should have been edited....<br />The set up was as follows: Steffi and Rhys were all loved up and out on a day trip with Tem tagging along. Tem hadn't been in the best mood to start with and being the third wheel was obviously unnerving her a little bit even if she uttered the following line in jest: <br /><i>"God you guys are sickening. I'm getting diabetes just looking at you"</i><br />Now I know it's sort of funny and meant in a less than serious manner but just think what it would be like if you had diabetes and read a line like that with someone kinda demeaning the seriousness of your condition... I think I wouldn't have been as bothered by this if this wasn't a book that was really doing a relatively nice job of writing the anxiety issues of Steffi and was shining light on what it must be like growing up deaf... I guess I just expected a little better from a book that was proudly showing characters with MH health issues that it shouldn't then have kinda belittled another type of illness. This isn't some darkly sardonic book with black humour that pushes the boundaries. This is a light teen romance with some grittier moments. That comment was unnecessary and could have been edited to maybe say something like 'you guys are so sugary sweet you could cause a tooth ache'. I'm not a writer obvs so not that exact line! Just something a little more innocuous. <br /><br />On a whole I really did love this and I do recommend it to anyone looking for a light teen romance with a more realistic feel than the standard cutesy YA fare that's out there.<br /><br /><b>three and a half stars</b> rounded to four </span>
  <a data-text-id="7173235137450418260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1872131810" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1872131810" />
    <a title="Dana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7632558-dana"><img alt="Dana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522963716p2/7632558.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1872131810?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana" href="/user/show/7632558-dana">Dana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7632558-dana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7632558-dana?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7632558-dana?shelf=borrow">borrow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7632558-dana?shelf=is-it-just-me">is-it-just-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7632558-dana?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7632558-dana?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7632558-dana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7632558-dana?shelf=satellite-mind">satellite-mind</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1872131810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16766596127989411766">I suppose that I should have known going into this that a book about a mute girl would have a lot of internal dialogue, but wow. <br/><br/>I mean, again it makes sense but I found it to be a bit grating at times. Especially a mute girl with anxiety issues and yeah....lots of verbal diarrhea. I suppose it was realistic, but it would have been nice if it was trimmed a bit. Still... in all fairness the premise of a romance between a girl with selective mutism and a deaf boy was very intriguing. <br/><br/>I always like</span>
  <span id="freeText16766596127989411766" style="display:none">I suppose that I should have known going into this that a book about a mute girl would have a lot of internal dialogue, but wow. <br /><br />I mean, again it makes sense but I found it to be a bit grating at times. Especially a mute girl with anxiety issues and yeah....lots of verbal diarrhea. I suppose it was realistic, but it would have been nice if it was trimmed a bit. Still... in all fairness the premise of a romance between a girl with selective mutism and a deaf boy was very intriguing. <br /><br />I always like reading about people that deal with different issues than my own. It was interesting to get a small glimpse into the deaf world. It would have been nicer if the book felt a little less preachy about it, but I can see how easy it is to make a subject that a lot of people don't have a huge understanding of into a ranty “ 10 Things not to say to a deaf person” book. <br /><br />In all fairness the preachiness wasn't a HUGE part of the book, but I did find myself rolling my eyes a bit during those parts as it felt a bit pretentious. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30971706.Things_I_Should_Have_Known" title="Things I Should Have Known by Claire LaZebnik" rel="nofollow noopener">Things I Should Have Known</a> did a much better job at enlightening the reader about a sensitive subject without coming across as overbearing. <br /><br />As for the romance I did like it for the most part, it made sense that the two protagonist would be drawn together and it went at a pretty realistic pace for teenagers. <br /><br />I did enjoy this book overall, it had a unique premise and if you have the patience for a bit of talking down to I think you might enjoy this.<br /><br /><b>Buy, Borrow or Bin Verdict: Borrow</b><br /><br />Check out more of my reviews <a href="https://satellitemind.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a><br /><br /><br />Note: I received this book for free in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16766596127989411766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ESIhSkdJfwWxde4zxsiZzyAjPen8Z5uyvjbwRDAw8Y4kSDVYXEVtnJt5QamhmBeEgzK1pXYfW4r1jexlegXfLQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OHHRNUdZX4vJBuV6naVqpRdLKoHF9+Th9nSDrKrWOR8NG8UnXFVNEuMKSuD69eTutFqizU+PJNm9z5+N4OMXvA==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/50647819-a-quiet-kind-of-thunder">Quotes from A Quiet Kind of T...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Panic attacks are a lot like being drunk in some ways, you lose self-control. You cry for seemingly no reason. You deal with the hangover long into the next day.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/8200488-panic-attacks-are-a-lot-like-being-drunk-in-some">41 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Here are three separate but similar things: shyness, introversion and social anxiety. You can have one, two or all three of these things simultaneously. A lot of the time people thing they're all the same thing, but that's just not true. Extroverts can be shy, introverts can be bold, and a condition like anxiety can strike whatever kind of social animal you are. <br /><br />Lots of people are shy. Shy is normal. A bit of anxiety is normal. Throw the two together, add some brain-signal error - a NO ENTRY sign on the neural highway from my brain to my mouth perhaps, though no one really knows - and you have me.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/8200473-here-are-three-separate-but-similar-things-shyness-introversion-and">32 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/50647819-a-quiet-kind-of-thunder">More quotes&hellip;</a>
